Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And the ancients called it "cure contuse," which is that you make behind the patient who has this disease the hair on his forehead be cut, then you make III incisions on the forehead equally according to the length of the forehead; and let one of the incisions as if II do throughout the forehead downwards until the nose, and the other two on each side above the temples, and beware of cutting into the arteries that are on both sides above the temples; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the II mandibles, and let each wound be the quantity of III fingers across; then have ready a piece of sponge and much cloth for wiping the blood, then place the spatumile sharp from both sides as this is its form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision which is above the temple until the second incision; and scrape off all the skin that is between the II cuts to the surface of the skull which is on the bone, then do likewise from the middle incision until the other second one, and then extract with this spatumile.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Insert into the first fissure the instrument which is called "cultellaire", and it is very well cutting on one side, and on the other side it is smooth, not cutting, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the cutting side towards the soft flesh of the heart, and the smooth side towards the bone, and insert it until it reaches the middle fissure.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous up to where it opens into the heart, and then make another incision in the middle fissure up to the other side; and then extract blood evenly, and press the area for blood clots; then place a piece of old cotton in each fissure, and cover with cloths moistened in wine and oil and honey, and guard against abscesses forming; on the third day loosen the bandage, and apply large poultices of vinegar, then treat with basilicon ointment mixed with rose oil, and other treatments used for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the rheum of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When catarrh frequently affects someone, and you see the eyes swollen and small, with vision weakening, and the whites of the eyes inflamed; and the hair falls out, and in the head there is pain from ague, and the patient sneezes; then by these symptoms you know that those substances and that catarrh come only from many veins, and if the mucus present is such, this is it.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you instruct the patient to lie with their back against their forehead, then make a large incision across the forehead, and another from ear to ear.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And start from the incision at the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision go up to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move when chewing; and when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, and then separate between the two edges of the incision and put old cotton there, and bandage it with linen; then place over damp cloths in wine and oil, and guard against hot abscesses; when it is removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat it with substances that promote healing, which cause tissue regeneration.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In such a manner: take two parts of wheat flour, and four parts of colophony, and make a poultice; and apply it to these wounds to generate flesh throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the blocking of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that falls into the ears is one of the four things: grains, animals, stones from mines or similar things such as iron; seeds, such as peas, beans, and lentils; or flowing substances such as water and pus and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When a stone or any other object that does not fit into the ear and does not grow in the ear falls into it, place the ear towards the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, then drop a little bit of violet oil or sesamum oil on it, and proceed with extraction; and make them sneeze with powdered substances, and plug their nostrils when they are about to sneeze, and place around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and keep the ear above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often the stone will come out through this treatment; and if it does not come out, use delicate forceps, which are described here:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the forceps, that is good; if not, use fine double-ended forceps; and if it does not come out with that, make a small fishhook of silk and insert its tip into the ear canal firmly, and plug the area around the hook with soft wax so that no air can enter through the hook; then pull it out forcefully, as often it will come out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this manner, take glutinous material which birds use to line their nests, and place a small instrument properly fitted for the task inside some of it, and wrap a little cotton around it; then press the glutinous substance against the stone or whatever is present, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she cannot escape from all these things that we have said, then hurry to cut the ear like an abscess below so that chills and spasms may come; and the manner of cutting is that you make the patient bleed from the cephalic vein according to the measure of his strength, then seat the patient between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear in the fat or hanging part; and let the cut be as crescent-shaped until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your power, and suck quickly with your mouth; and cure him until he is well.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if this grain is inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer a thin poultice according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer an incision of that swelling.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think the swelling is moist due to moisture from the ear, until you have made many incisions; then extract with fine forceps and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is gentle.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case of acute illness that falls into the ear, the patient should use sneezing powder first, and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lie down on that same side where the illness is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	if it comes out because of that, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	if that is not the case, take many stones according to the length of your thumb and light ones, and warm them slightly over the fire; then put one stone in the patient’s ear, and hold it there with another foot away on the other side, and press against the stone in the ear with another stone; do not stop placing one stone upon another until all the fluid comes out, and thus it will come out completely; and if you wish, take a reed, put one end of it in the patient’s ear, and hold the other end over fire until the softer part is burned; then repeat this with other reeds until all the fluid comes out, as we have said about the stones.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the removal of the creature, if it is small like a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is large enough to be felt, remove it with tweezers; and this is the easiest thing to take out that may be in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from the ears, when you treat them as we have said in the division and in the treatment of distillations, and the cure does not help, then it is necessary that you look at the ear in the sun: if any worms appear, take them out with fine forceps, and if none are seen, use the method described here:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And insert the finer end into the ear according to the amount of pain the patient feels, then gradually form it all along the canal; do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not come out, plug around the canal with cotton as I said about stones; and if they do not emerge as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven effective against worms, which you will find in the treatment of distillations; and distil your oils and medicines into the ear using this instrument, the form of which is shown as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let it be of silver or brass narrow at the small openings, and above that cover for dripping; and to press inside the distillation use an instrument of brass well made for this, and if you wish take a razor and wrap around the tip appropriately with cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicine you want in the tube, and let the tube be in the ear; then put inside the razor all over the cotton, and press with your hand gently until the oil is distilled to the bottom of the ear; and let the patient feel it within, and keep the distillations a little heated by fire as when you distil into the ear; and beware that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the congestion of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	Some children are born without any hole in their ears; and this same thing happens to adults due to a stoppage of the wound, or flesh grown inside the ear, and these blockages sometimes occur deep in the ear, such that one cannot see them; and sometimes it is necessary for the hole to be made to come out, and then one can see it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	The one that occurs deep inside, which cannot be seen, requires difficult treatment in many cases, and for the one you can see, you should place the patient's ear towards the sun; and look inside: if you see inflammation clearly, then proceed with this spatula as shown here.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and cutting in front and smooth at the back so that it does not hurt the ear; if the inflammation is of flesh grown within or on the ear, then hold it with fine forceps, and gently scrape away all the tissue.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if there is an obstruction in the ear, take a fine and light razor and heat it slightly over fire, then place it in the flesh of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the obstruction and the patient feels pain in the ear, pierce it gently, and be careful not to damage the nerves of the ear; then place a tent in the ear according to the width of the opening, and apply Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for as many days as it takes for the wound to heal, or take a tent and moisten it in rose water, and sprinkle powdered vitriol on top; and if you see that the ear is swollen, then you must remove the tent and replace it with another one moistened in cerate made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling subsides; then continue to treat it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, dip a sponge and cloths in cold water, and place them on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the bleeding which are in the treatment of hemorrhages.
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This althethum that comes from the eyes when they are moist and dry, you must stretch them with tongs and forceps, and cut off a piece of its root with a scalpel; then place over the spot vitriol ground up.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without removing it, you cauterize with the lentil cautery and then cauterize after incision with mues; and many times they repair where some part remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of hailstones
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times things come from the eyes that resemble hailstones in form and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "hail," and it is a collection of thick moisture above and below the membrane; the treatment is as follows: observe if the hail moves to one side or another, and it is easy to know; then take them out widely, then gently scrape each part, then take them with forceps, and cut them.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cut it without piercing slightly the skin, do not cause any harm to the patient; and if the wound is large, sew it up with a stitch, and treat it until it heals; and if it is small, do not force anything, for the ointment will heal it quickly and regenerate flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the grain is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, turn over the skin, and extract the grain with forceps, and cut and press from both sides; and if the skin is removed by incision, it does not cause any harm; and when the grain is removed, lift the eye with salt water, and treat the area that regenerates flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the grease of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that is produced in the membranes above the pupils, and this happens more often to children than to some people, and it causes them great pain in their eyes, and they get catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because tears hasten to their eyes; and for this reason they lie on their backs immediately, and sleep like that, and their membranes below their eyebrows are moistened by exinach which appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press that place with your thumb and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is that the patient places his head on your hand; then take one cloth of linen, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity it contains exinach for each part, then place it over him; and press with your thumbs from both sides so that the exinach is assembled within the circle; then cut open the moisture with a sharp spatula making a slit no larger than the incision made when opening a vein; and make an incision through completely until you reach the exinach; and in many cases, the exinach comes out from the slit, according to the form of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Draw it then in one piece of ripped cloth between your two fingers when removing it, and move your hand right and left until it is spread; and be careful not to jam into the crevice, so that you do not come to completely cover the spatumile up to the eye, so that you do not injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the excrement does not appear at the beginning of the opening, then gently widen the opening slightly until it appears; then remove it as we have said, then moisten cloths with oil and water, and place them on the area, and bandage it.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And there are people who grind salt and apply it to corrupt the moisture that remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat him until he is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he comes to the place of an abscess that is hot, treat him with poultices to alleviate it until he is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of the eyelids
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow in places other than those intended by nature on the eyelids and become entangled, they harm the eyes and cause various diseases such as habitual tears and inflammation of the eyelids and conjunctiva, to the point where it can lead to the destruction of the eyes; and the treatment is according to four methods: either by cautery with fire altogether, or by medicine accordingly as it was mentioned before in the chapter on cautery, and also by incision and suturing, or by cauterization, as I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you place the head of the patient in your lap, then turn the paper of the eye towards your left hand; if it turns, it is good; if not, insert a needle along all the thread; and let this be near the margin of the paper where the hair grows among these hairs, and draw the thread above all the paper, and turn it to the razor; then cut in the part below the paper, below the adjacent hairs, up to the entire spectacle area from the large tear duct to the small; then remove the thread, and place under the paper a small tent of cotton and cloth, then sign on the paper a figure of an anchor, like the leaf of myrtle, and nonetheless it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you wish to raise the paper which is designed for all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there is one who needs it cut in great quantity of the paper according to how much the paper is softened; then make across all the spatulate on both lines that you have marked, and begin from the large tear up to small; and let one of the incisions be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert the needle into one of the two corners of the wound, then skin it entirely; then sew together the two edges with a single fine thread on a needle, and wipe away the blood, and make adhere the excess threads around both eyebrows to certain sticky substances if you wish to do this; and if not, pay no mind, then leave the stitches and the threads until three or four days; then cure the wound without stitching of drying and binding materials because the paper rises suddenly from the wound and its coming together, but the stitching is soft (as the ancients say), and these are works without fear; and there is another way: which is that you mark the paper with a shape like the leaf of myrtle, as we have described, at three inches apart according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut those which rise above the small forces evenly according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the forceps, and the things are not equal, take a needle with thread, and place it in the figure; then place another thread beside the large artery, and the second thread beside the small one, and tie both threads evenly; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin on which you have marked, as we have described, then suture the two lips of the wound together, and heal until it is healthy; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar soothing ointments; but sometimes the hair from the membrane is turned: then it is necessary to use what we have said about the incision; however, the sutures in both cases are more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of the canthi is as follows: you should turn the paper and cut it according to what I have said, then make two canthi by art, and two fine threads as long as the paper and the width of the spatula are; and tie at the two corners where you hold the threads; then gently bring together one and the other above the part that sticks out from the paper around the eye, and pull the two canthi firmly from both sides; leave it thus for several days, and the skin which is pulled will die off and heal and grow, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, then cut with force, and treat until it is healed; and when the wound is sealed, the paper will be lifted, and no more hair will grow there; and this is the form of the two canthi that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you take a fine needle and put a thin silk thread underneath; then join the edges and tie one to the other finely, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then arrange in the socket another fine silk thread briefly, and tie the ends of the thread; then have the patient place his head on your hand; and keep it near the sun so that the work is clear, for this is a delicate and small work, then pierce the needle throughout the socket at the root of the hair alongside, and make it pierce into the membrane quickly as you draw it over the natural hair; then pull out the hair up to the socket, and place in the socket that hair if there are one or two or three or more; then withdraw your hand until the hairs come out completely from the socket with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hair is treated and does not come out with it, draw the needle back along all the thread that you have inserted until the hair comes out from the opening above and you can see it by sight; then pull out the needle and leave a thread in place for two days or three, until the hair grows in its place and the flesh grows over; and if the hair is short, match one long hair from the natural ones, and raise it with the one where you left it, until it is raised and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	from the pus of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or pus comes in the eye, it happens in two ways: one naturally, and the other unnaturally.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by sudden wound, or incision, or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of the work is that you should split the wound, separate its edges, and place linen strips inside, keeping it dressed until it heals; and it is not appropriate to use in its treatment things that dry out and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the illness will return worse than before; but use things that soften it, such as fenugreek; and bathe with water or a decoction of flax seeds, and apply ointment made from dissolved mutton fat mixed with some oil, and wrap a cloth around it, and treat it thus.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you guard against it not healing according to its former form; and these works which we have mentioned are nothing other than remedies for this disease, so that it does not return according to its former form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is called "axacrati" in truth, and its nature and circumstances.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The circumstances arise from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things; and the method of treatment is that you take a needle, on which there should be double thread, and insert it into the flesh, and pierce starting from the left tear duct to the right, so that the thread passes through two points of the flesh; then stretch the flesh above all over the needle, and cover with one spatula width.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns according to what is required, it is good; if not, take the scraper and place it in the fissure, and turn the paper, and make II fissures on either side within the paper; and let the edges of the II fissures be at the II corners of the incision that you have made, and shape them so that when they are joined together, the figure is as the figure of a letter called «I griesche»; then remove that flesh according to the quantity that its sides are acute underneath, from what lies under the paper, then join the II separated parts with thread; then treat it with what we have said about softening medicines and tents until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a fissure or seam or cautery, it is necessary that you make a full fissure underneath the hairs of the paper, as stated above; then separate between the II leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one must perform the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and wise masters prepare their instruments with all their power so that they may bring back the figure to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what requires work and tools in various conditions.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the sudden swelling of the skin
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this swelling occurs in such a manner that the skin above is swollen with the white of the eye, and he cannot move or do his natural works, then you should place the tip of a razor under the skin, and lift it up; and stretch it with forceps, until you cut away what adheres to the delicate spatumile, which must not be too sharp or too cutting, so that the patient cannot endure the spatumile causing any injury to the eye; and make your incision, by which you peel off this assembly, lightly, so that the skin returns to its natural form; and heal entirely this assembly, and sometimes put in the eye a brine solution, and lift it with fresh water, and of milk; then place between the skin and the eye a pad of linen, and place on the eye wool moistened abundantly with egg white; and after three days use a poultice and soothing things until he is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail is according to two manners: one is nervous and similar to hard skin, and another which is not nervous, but is like white congealed moisture, so when it is touched by iron and one thinks to pinch it with pincers, it cannot be done; and both semblances begin near the large tear duct, and grows little by little until it covers all the sight and all the light and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the incision is that the patient places their head in your lap, then works the eyes; and lift the paper to your hand, then coil the nail with pincers slightly, and stretch it above; then take a needle, and put horsehair, or cow hair, or bull's hair on it, and strong thread; and double the point of the needle a little and pierce it into the nail, and pierce it all through the needle, and tie the nail with one thread and stretch it above, and shave off all the hair around the side of the nail which is near the tear duct and tie the hair to the root of the tear duct up to the head, then cut the remaining part at the base of the tear duct throughout the fine spatula and small forces, and leave the natural flesh of the tear duct so that by the incision there does not come forth tears habitually; and sometimes stretch the nail only on a needle and with thread as we have said; then shave off all the spatula under which is this form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And ensure that the spatula does not touch the tender flesh and break it, and that the probe is not pierced; after the incision, sprinkle a bit of ground sulfur into the eye, and from the preparation made with litharge, apply it until the next day; then treat it as needed until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerve-filled and you cannot insert the needle, and the forceps cannot enter, this condition of the nail is often treated with various medicines; and it grows as I have described in the section, and if you wish to cut it, proceed carefully with the patient's eye, and take a light, sharp spatula according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And raise the nail gently above, and if you see that it thins slightly and the tissue adheres to it, then drip from your mouth into the eye a preparation made of litharge and red ochre and ground sulfur, and plug the eye until the next day; then continue with the other work according to this same method until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If anything is contrary in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then let it be, and treat the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh from the eyelid harms the eye greatly, then suspend it at the corner and cut a part but not entirely so that no tears come out; then drip into the eye red choler which is made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows over the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	In some people's eyes, red flesh sometimes grows and covers the pupil, restrains it beneath the eyelids, and turns it outward, resembling a white rose; and the procedure is that the patient places their head on a clean surface, then the treatment of the eye begins. Use appropriate hooks to coil all this flesh, and support it with force; then cut the first layer, and continue cutting until you reach the end, being careful not to injure the eye during the work; make the incision in the way we described for the nail bed and small finger operations as illustrated after this chapter; when the incision is complete and all the flesh has been removed, apply salve or grind it into a paste where you can drip red choler and similar corrosive medicines; then place cotton soaked in egg white on top of the eye to prevent a hot abscess; if anything remains and there is suspicion of a hot abscess, leave the eye alone and treat the abscess with soothing remedies for a hot abscess; then return to your work until it heals, and similarly handle any flesh attached to the eye by this method.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, it is necessary that you treat each weak eye by the natural way; and by the accidental way, using iron work; and do not put your hand into any of these works until you see that this member can bear that work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Red veins that cover the eye cause discomfort in its work and weaken the eye all day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Therefore, it is necessary first to check if the eye, in which the ailment exists, is alone and there is no other disease except this ailment; then treat it in such a manner: instruct the patient to place his head on your hand, then suspend those veins along the entire tendon according to your knowledge, and let the tendons be fine double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let two lancets be arranged in gradations along the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then, as you apply force to those veins subtly, and wipe the blood hour after another, until you see those veins withdraw from the eye; and be careful not to injure the eye with the points of the spathes, and perform this work at noon facing the sun, and be very diligent in your work so that you do not miss any of those veins; and when you have done this, then drop into the eye green and red collyrium to corrupt what remains of the sore.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you do not have the power to collect all of this at that hour, then apply a poultice on the eye with things that ease the pain of the eyes, and leave it for several days until the pain is eased and be assured there is no hot abscess, then restart according to this manner as described earlier until he is healed; and this is the form of applying force.
de la fistule de l’oil	Of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The physician calls this type of fistula "arissati": when you treat it with cautery and hot medicine as I have said before, and it does not heal, then there is pus that you must incise at the abscess, where it should be opened, and drain all the moisture that is inside until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and darkness, then remove it with all the instruments that are shown here; it is called "aspre chief," and should be made of iron bent into a head like a file as it appears in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the site of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two hands and press gently until you know that the corruption is removed; do this several times, then restore the area with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the flesh is sealed and new flesh grows, and the body of the bowel remains sealed, and it stays thus for forty days, and does not renew itself nor become an abscess, and no bad accident occurs, know that it is healthy; if this is not the case, there is another intention to bring the fistula back to the anus according to this form: which is to uncover the bone a second time with iron, and by using dry medicines, and when it is uncovered take one fork according to this form, and let the head of iron be at three angles, and let the shaft be slender up to the top as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone near the lamina, and move your hand from the eye one inch, then turn the fork completely until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it because wind enters if he holds his hand over his anus; and then restore the area with dry medicines as I have taught you, and when new flesh grows and hardens the tissue, remove the matter to the anus; this is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the discharge of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye is fully open and there is no disturbance or reduction in vision, you must bind the patient; then treat it, then apply cups to suck without cutting, then place on the eye a preparation made of boxwood, aloes, incense, and saffron; and then extract the eye, and apply plasters over bandages and cloths. The method for the cloths is that you take soft cloths and fold each one four times, and then lay them one upon another according to the size needed by the eye. Then press it down with a firm bandage, and continue using the cups to suck without cutting; then remove the cups and leave the eye bound day and night, and if the dressing becomes loose, you must tighten it much; then after a day and night, remove the dressing, and if you see the eye healing, that is good; if not, repeat the plasters and cloths and binding and suction until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	from the tearing of a vein
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a disruption comes to the vein of the eye, it opens up, and there appears pus like resin seeds, which is frightening to see; then if you wish to treat it, you place one needle at the root of the part below, then insert another needle where the double thread from the eyebrow part is; and pierce it, leaving the first needle according to its position; then cut the area of the double thread and tie a part of the eye around it tightly, then extract the needle and apply linen soaked in abundance with egg; and leave it until the thread falls off with the eye vein, then cure the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restrained by the eye vein all around with a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye shows great appearance, then pierce it with a fine spatula that comes from the side of the eye, and let the milky moisture flow out and lower the eye; then extract it until it is healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the socket of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing but an accumulation in the eye, resembling water dripping down, yet it is not actually water; and the manner of its appearance is that you seat the patient on a prepared and straight chair, then take his head between your hands from both sides, and move it until you see the accumulation come up to your eyes; then if it remains there without descending and obscuring the light, know that it is indeed water, and if the descent of the accumulation does not appear as we have described.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Seat the patient between your hands, then take the spatula and make an incision through the corneous membrane in the direction of the conjunctiva and cornea, until the pus comes out; and when it has come out, drip warm honey mixed with water or fenugreek boiled with honey into the eye, then treat it further as necessary until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the eyes' fluids
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have described the appearances of the fluids in the division and what is necessary for piercing them; act according to the health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	You should seat the patient between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun, and with the healthy eye held tightly; then place the paper of the affected eye in your left hand if it is the left eye, or in your right hand if it is the right eye; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument called "almagda," or in your left hand, if the eye is right; then place the tip of the instrument near the cornea by the thickness of a thread on that white part of the eye towards the lower tear duct, and insert the "almagda" carefully, turning your hand until it pierces the white of the eye, and feel when the almagda reaches the empty space; and it is necessary for the length of the path of the almagda to be perfectly equal to the distance from the plum-pit up to the end of the black part; this is the cornea; you will see the bone on that paper through the clarity of the corneous membrane, then place the instrument where the fluid is, and press it out one way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the aqueous humor now descends, the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a short time, if the aqueous humor rises again, apply force with the instrument, and when it is firmly in place and does not rise further, gently extract with almagda by turning your hand little by little; then put a small amount of rock salt into the eye, and lift the eye from there.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then place around the outside of the eye plugs made of wool soaked in rose oil and an abundance of egg whites, and bind it with a healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, apply it with comminuted material mixed in abundance with egg whites.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, because there are some people who have eyes that are too hard, then you must take the instrument called “alberit”, here is its form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	Then pierce only the conjunctiva and do not go too deep, but proceed carefully; then insert the almagda as we have said; upon completion of the work, prepare for the patient a comfortable sleeping arrangement where he lies on his back in a dark place; be cautious of all movements, give him light food, and do not move his head to the right or left; bind him according to his disposition until the third day; then unbind him in that same dark place, test his vision, show him some objects, and then rebind him until the seventh day; it is not necessary to do this immediately during treatment or after incision now, but you should delay it because the fluid accumulates quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If abscesses appear, that you loosen the eye before the seventh day, and direct it to him who alleviates abscesses; and when it is pacified, then loosen the sight and place on it a small cloth to cover for some days, and let it be immediately in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then leave the house gradually and return to his normal activities; and know that no student should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Iraque, who told us that in their country they make almond-shaped incisions for which water is sucked out, but nevertheless I have never seen any such thing in our land, nor have I ever read about it in ancient books; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of the forms of almonds, because those who do not recognize them see them; and they are properly of brass:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the heads of these be of the same subtlety, and the rear in three acute angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes flesh on the nose grows in various shapes, some of which appear as many-legged scorpions; and there are such cases where it has a swollen red appearance, and there is also smooth skin of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In the case of that flesh which is smooth and not swollen, you should seat the patient between your hands facing the sun; work his nostrils, apply the lancet to those parts, and draw them out thinly; then hold as much as you can sustain with a fine sharp spatula on one side, until you know that all the flesh has been removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains anything that you cannot cut, then treat it with all the instruments subtly and gently, so nothing is left; and if without penetrating too far, an abscess bursts, then cover it as is appropriate; and if these are malignant abscesses, then hurry and cauterize until the blood ceases to flow and all the flesh is removed, then apply clean water or vinegar or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the urine flows and moisture reaches up to the palate, know that it is safe; and if moisture does not penetrate as it should, know there is flesh grown on the bone above where the instrument cannot cut: then you must insert a thick thread of flax, and tie it tightly with knots, leaving between each knot enough space for one finger at least; and place the patient's head in the thread at its narrowest part, and pull through smelling until it comes out through the mouth; and many times children at school do this, and it is an easy thing for one who wants to do it; then hold the end that comes out from the nose with one hand, and the other end that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and pull apart gradually as you feel what is in the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you know that the new tissue has corrupted the flesh, then pull out the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nose as before; do this for III days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of the flesh; and then place a silver chain in the nose for some days until it is healed, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, through which oils and medicines are dripped into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And whether it is of silver or brass, it should resemble an open lamp, like a chain, and the conduit should be similar; and if you wish, make a closed chain, and the instruments should be full for purging the head; and let it have one handle at the top to hold when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh upon the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" is born on the head of the nose, and it grows and becomes large in time, such that it is visible to the eye; and for this reason you must cut it at the beginning, remove it entirely, then apply the cautery or hot medicine to its place; and if one delays cutting it until it is large, be cautious if it is hard, of a bad color, and lacking sensation: do not touch it with iron because it is an entrenched abscess, for when you cut it even once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not of a bad color, and you see that one can entirely cut it out, then empty the patient of blood without fear, and treat the place with drying and binding substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the skin is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when solutions for continuity come in one of these cartilage works, there is little benefit, except in some men.
