then place your middle finger in where the testicle is situated, between the white fat under the foreskin and the second layer, and separate what's behind the testicle from the second layer; then move it with your right hand into the heart of the scrotum, stretch the hard fat up to your left hand, and lift the testicle towards the waist; instruct the assistant to stretch the testicle upwards and undo the bandage at the back; check if any part of the intestines is wrapped around the hard fat, and if you find anything, move it under the belly; then take a needle with a thick thread made from ten strands, and insert it into the rear part of the fatty tissue behind the foreskin; after the waist, cut the threads so there remain four strands; then arrange them one above the other in a cross shape, and tie up the fatty tissue we mentioned under the skin of the scrotum with a strong thread from both sides; then wrap the remaining threads and tie them firmly from both sides, so that no foreign matter can enter, preventing abscesses; then apply another bandage according to the first long one for two fingers' width, and after these two bandages leave exposed the fatty tissue under the scrotum by a hand's breadth; then cover everything else according to the round shape of the testicle; then cut from the part under the skin of the groin until reaching the unscarred area and the bowe as we said earlier; then apply wet linen soaked in oil on the wound, and place the bandage we mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white vein that we have mentioned is cauterized after the incision, out of fear of bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this often happens, and let the ligature remain until it falls off by itself; and if it delays in falling, soak it with warm water, and put on what we have said, until it falls off; then treat the wound with another method, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of flesh hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case, I have never seen anyone dare to treat it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is done like the condition involving both the intestine and the abdominal wall, in such a way that you bind the vessels above the navel lightly on the back side; then cut into it, and treat the abscess with what we have described, until the vessels fall off; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a rupture occurs in the groin area, as we have said, and it is evident; and no part of the intestines descends to the thighs, and if they do descend, this is dangerous, and requires immediate attention at all times; and yet if it remains too long in this state, the wound or the hernia will worsen until the intestines descend further; and this happens due to the extension of the hernia area which we have mentioned, because it first extends, then softens and swells up visibly; and the treatment for this is by cautery, as we have previously stated; sometimes it is treated with iron in this manner: the patient lies supine on their back between your hands, then cover the swollen part of the hernia with a cloth about three fingers wide according to its size; then extract the herniated tissue beneath the skin that follows, then take the thread and place it over the visible area of the hernia; press firmly against the middle of the abdomen, then sew both sides together tightly; then pull out the head of the thread, do not cut the hernia or stretch the skin further as I have told you in the treatment for intestinal prolapse; then treat it according to the methods used for wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, then dress and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The tissue is tense, and there is no appearance of tearing in the rupture, and the cauterization is cold in this area, and closer to safety.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of softening the skin of the scrotum
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	The skin of the scrotum is often softened in some men because the tissues inside are softened, and it appears milky; and when one wishes to treat it, have the patient lie on his back, and cut the soft skin over the natural skin; then join the two lips with a seam, and if you wish, sew together the excess soft skin at three seams or four firmly; then cut between the seams, and treat it as other wounds until it is healed, and stitch the thread.
dou chastrement	of the treatment
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	You know that castration is forbidden in our law, and for this reason I would prefer not to speak of it in this book; yet it is necessary for two reasons: one is so that the physician knows how to respond when asked and knows the treatment; and the other, because we often need to castrate certain animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say then that castration is performed in two ways: either by traction or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the method where we perform castration by traction, we have the animal sit in hot water until the testicles are softened and hanging down; then grasp them with your hand until they are retracted and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of the castration of animals: you should anesthetize the animal, and press the skin over its testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory bandage, and cut through each testicle in one stroke when you have properly skinned them; and leave some of the fatty tissue and the delicate fat that is on the vessels; and this method of castration is gentler than that which is done by traction, because with traction there may remain a part of the testicles accidentally, causing the animal to desire lust; then treat the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermpheidry is in two manners for men: one is that between the two testicles there appears as clearly as the figure of a woman's nature, with hair, and sometimes urination occurs there.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other method is for women, and place upon the wrist as thick as a rod and two fingers.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for both men and women is that you cut away all adhering tissues, and treat them as other wounds; in the second method, for men whose urine sprays over the skin of the genitals, there is no specific treatment.
de la tentigene	of the tension or strain
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tentigene is a tissue adhering to the natural part, so that it appears too ugly; and some women have it as large as a hand, and this is how it is treated.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You should dye the excess of the tentigene with your hand or fingers, and cut it lightly; do not go too deep, so that no blood flows, then treat it as you would other wounds until it is healed; and for another part that arises at the mouth of the vagina, remove it, and sometimes it may bleed, and it resembles a horn, hence they called it by the ancients "horn disease.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary to treat it as we have said about tendinitis, and care for it until it is healed.
de erratique	erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	It is erratic when the nature of a woman's body is not perceived, or the passage is small; and it is by nature at birth, or caused by illness that has come upon her; or due to added flesh, or thin or thick membrane, which forms perfectly in the womb, or in the ribs, or elsewhere; and it prevents conception, childbirth, and perhaps menstruation; and knowledge of this is determined by examining the aperture.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If constipation is appearing soon, either use two or use the right method.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is of subtle syfac [a type of swelling or inflammation], and it is near the two leaves [likely referring to anatomical locations], hurry, and do this: place your two fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread; then stretch the two areas firmly until the subtle syfac is flat, and over the swelling; then take linen, and moisten it in oil, and apply it to the area, and have the woman rest face down each day so that she may not sweat.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the syfac is hard and thick, then you should cut it with an instrument similar to a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is of flesh growth, suspend it by a thread and cut it; and have medicines that staunch blood, such as vinegar, dragon's blood, incense, along with an abundance of egg whites; then cover the wound with a piece of flax large enough so that the wound cannot close; and thus keep covered for some time, and treat the wound with bandages until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when flesh is infected in the wound, it must be cut according to this method, except for embedded abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For in the wound where there is an embedded abscess, one must not cut it open.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are protrusions of veins that usually occur without cause, and when hemorrhoids become old they turn hard; we have already described their appearances and signs in the division, and I will say here those that can be cured.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that when hemorrhoids and hard growths are fully formed in the wound and do not respond to sensation, they cannot be cured by cautery.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who have the mouth of the ulcer, which can be felt, are those who can be treated by scraping.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore, you must place the woman in a cold room, then remove the altar with tongs, and cut it at its roots; then apply powdered medicines that constrict blood, such as oak bark and dragon's blood and frankincense, and similar things. Then place her feet against the wall for an hour, then put her in cold water; if bleeding continues, make her sit in a decoction of sumac, pomegranate peel, gallnuts, and similar things, and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and grease, and use it to apply a plaster on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if the bleeding stops, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, have the patient undergo cupping on the back and breasts without injuring them; then take flax, soak it in plantain juice or elderberry juice with old wine, and apply it to the area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has rested, treat the area with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red and resembles a hard head, so it must be cut as I said about the thulul; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	for abscesses of the flesh
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscesses occur in the flesh, such as cankers and stone abscesses and herpes and ulcers and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary that I speak in this treatise about the hot abscess which comes in the marrow, which is not of those abscesses that are collected from the bowels; and if you wish to know the work of iron, look to see whether the abscess is sharp at the beginning of its arrival, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hurry to pierce it, but let it die until the pain subsides; and then make the patient sit on a chair, and have two small chairs where he can recline, and support his back and bring together his legs towards the side away from the thigh; and keep his thighs spread apart, and place his arms under his knees, and tie them securely with a good cloth; then give him some linseed oil to the right side of his chest, and there administer the instrument used to work on the mouth of the marrow, of which the form follows next; and it is necessary that when you intend to use this instrument, you insert its tip first to know the depth of the marrow, so that what enters inside the instrument does not exceed its proper depth and does not harm the patient; and if the instrument is larger, then cover the depth of the marrow with cloths so that the instrument does not hurt it; and he should place the cone of the instrument above and hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is open, and it is incised gently by hand, then you must cut off the top at the spatumile site; and when the pus is emptied out, it is necessary to put into the wound moist cloths soaked in rose oil or green oil; place the cloth over the wound towards the margin, and place on top of the margin and on the point clean wool wet with water or mallows that have been cooked; then cure after two days of ointment application as appropriate until it is healed; sometimes lift the margin and the wound by enema of water and honey, and then with water in which long arum roots and aristolochia are boiled; then return to the treatment with ointments.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is laid open in the margin, then you must avoid heating with iron, but treat it as we have said in the section.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is necessary first for the midwife to know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs if you see a woman pressing downwards, and desiring to smell the air: then you know that the child hastens to come forth; then you know that this birth is according to the natural figure, and the passage is under its head, and the afterbirth with it; and when you see these signs, it is necessary lightly to press her belly, so that the child may quickly issue; for when it descends under its head, the afterbirth comes with it, and the woman is cleansed of her superfluities by good care; and those who come forth otherwise do not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it sometimes comes upon its feet, and the body or head, and the hands, or upon her belly, or back, and is turned perhaps upon its neck, and by other bad figures; so it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in these things, and wary of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should help them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes down on its head by natural means, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and if her strength is weak, then make her sit on a stool, where women usually hold them; and prepare her nature with oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then place a small basin between her two thighs:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and cut the perineum, and make a small incision to allow the moisture within to flow out; and press on the woman's abdomen until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to administer an enema of fenugreek muscilaginous substance with sesame oil; then have her drink and sneeze from condisi, and keep her mouth and nose closed for one hour: now the child will come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands exit forcefully, then you must reset them gently bit by bit; and if they cannot enter, place the woman on a chair, and raise her feet up high; then lift the chair onto the ground, and steady the woman so she does not fall when standing up; and if the hands still cannot enter, and the child dies, cut the hands with the knife that is placed here beforehand, extract the child, and reset them equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of delivering the child onto its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes up on its feet, it is necessary to push it upwards; then turn it bit by bit until it is straight; then take one of its feet and stretch it bit by bit.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	When it jumps up to the thighs, command it to be grasped, and make it sneeze from conditon; if it jumps further, if God wills.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not go further as we have said, turn it little by little until it is according to its natural position.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it moves easily.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come out as we have said, take muscilagine of elder, and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and grind all in a mortar; then put the essence of the woman inside and outside this ointment, then make her sit in warm water up to below the ribs; when she is moistened below, apply an infusion of myrrh there, and let it stay for one hour; then make her sit on the commode, then make her sneeze and pinch her mouth and nose, and gently massage her abdomen, for the child now jumps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the child's birth upon his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this manner, place its hands gently bit by bit; then lay it on its back, and let the feet hang down, and have it lying on the bed; and bend its hands bit by bit, and then take its hands to its belly, and remove the cushions underneath until it is prepared downward; and if the child does not jump, lift its feet and move them forward, then move its belly upward, then place your hands there; and bring out the child bit by bit; and instruct the woman to hold on as much as possible until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the birth of the child who emerges with one hand hanging out
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary for the engineer to return the hand: if it cannot be returned, make the woman stand and walk; if she cannot walk, lie her on the bed and straighten her legs completely; then administer the muscillation as I have described; and if she does not give birth, make her sit on a chair, then study how to return the hand; and hold the child according to its natural form, and make her sneeze, and command her to grasp firmly until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the exit of the child onto its neck, and have her spread out her hands, and her face turned towards her mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary for the baby to hold her hand, then turn it little by little, and move it gently; and when it is even, apply the natural muscillation of heat and oil as we have said, then command her to move it little by little; and when you have done this, make her sit on a chair, and command her to grasp firmly; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same manner to the entire second part
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to applying force in this manner to the entire second part, cut the second part with your nail until the moisture is emptied; and if the child can be brought up on its face and neck, cut from the mouth so that it is not retained, and move the child; then place the child inside as it should be, and instruct the woman to grasp it several times: then gently extract it.
de l’issue des gemelz	on the outcome of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	You should know that twins are often born, and sometimes three or four are born; and this is not a strange thing, and it can happen.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are strange things, and do not live, if one can call them that; I know they multiply, and are separated by the surface which divides them, which is attached to the bud; and sometimes they issue as naturally as other shoots, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they emerge roughly, treat them as we have said, and let the nurse be subtle, and do quickly and gently what she does; and act as it is necessary for health.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the month I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more up to XV, and are completely formed in the shape of a child according to the measurement of the wise physician, and it is necessary for the nurse to know all this, because similar things may happen; so act accordingly.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman of the dead child in her womb, as I said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to work with your hands; then it is necessary that you know if the woman has good health, and has no accident or fear of death; then the woman must be laid on her back, with her knees bent downwards, and her legs raised; and the assistant holds the towel from two sides, where she lies on the bed so that it does not touch below the child; then smear her mouth with marish oil mixed moistly with muscilla of hellebore and fenugreek and flax seeds, then anoint her palms with these oils and these muscillae; then gently place your hands in the marish, then find a suitable place to make the incision where the child is prepared to come down headfirst; if it descends feet first, insert the needle between ribs or at other appropriate places; and you must hold the needle in your right hand, and put the loop between two fingers of your left hand, gently move your hands, then insert the needle at one of these places until it reaches the empty space; and this is the form of the needle:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then place against the other hook, or a third one if you need it, so that the extraction is equal; and then spread them equally by moving from side to side, for the muscles to come out, and let the hooks be toothed to hold the muscles, as shown in this form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, anoint the edge with some of his two oils, and place it in that part, and pull out the other part; and if any part remains, attach this hook to a higher position, and do so until everything comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and he cannot return it for grasping, you must wrap around the finger until it completely comes out; then place a bandage at the joint of the palm or at the base, and similarly you must do this with the other hand, and on both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of the child is large and it is tight in the passage, or there is an acute accumulation in the head, then you must pierce with a pointed spatula between your two fingers, cut open the head, and extract the fluid; or shave it with the instrument called "almidach," of which the form comes with the instruments in the chapter that follows this one; and likewise do if the child has a large natural head; and then pull out the bones with forceps, and if the head jumps out and is stuck to the forceps, cut them off so that the moisture coming from the pus passage can flow; and if it cannot come out, cut it in pieces as much as you can; and if it swells in the belly or under the ribs, then you must pierce it until the moisture runs.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then the traction is light, and the adjustment to the mouth of the womb is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if he is tight in the abdomen or breast, then you must stretch him with a sling wrapped around the hand; and cut the abdomen or breast until the moisture that is there flows out; and if another part is removed, and the head remains, then put your hand in perfectly to the mouth of the womb, and pull it up to the mouth of the womb; then put your thumb or two fingers in, and pull firmly; and if the mouth of the womb is narrow due to a hot abscess that has come, then there must be no work done, but rather moisture and fat should be administered; and administer plasters, and apply them with liquids that soften and moisten.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on its side, and you can make it even, then treat it as we have said about the living child; and if one has no power over it, then cut it into pieces, and leave nothing of the second skin.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, treat it as we have said about large abscesses that come with fever; and if bleeding occurs, apply cold compresses, and then treat with other remedies.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whom the fetus had died in her womb, then another was conceived after that one, and even this other one died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, abscesses came in her mouth, and it swelled so much that it burst, and began to severely rot.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat it, and I pondered long, and could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a plaster of strong attraction, and out came one bone, and after several days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled greatly, for there are no bones in the abdomen.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it must be the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I examined the wound and extracted many bones, until the woman was in a much better condition; and she remained with me for a long time, and occasionally a bit of fluid would come out from there; and I recall this chapter only because when masters encounter something unusual, they should seek to understand it.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to return the joint to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Here follows the form of the binder, which the books have; and for two turns to the two shoulders of the two arms.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the horns should be finer than the binder, and made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the shaft should be two fingers wide, and the margin of the trees one finger, and a length of one palm and a half; and between the two arms there should be two fixtures of the same wood, which are securely fastened in each, about half a palm long or slightly more; and these two fixtures are positioned at the mouth of the joint to open when the two horns are turned.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony wood or boxwood, resembling pincers; and let it have two heads with attachments as you see, one palm long and two fingers wide; and when you wish to open the mouth with this instrument, seat the woman on a bed, her feet hanging down and legs spread apart, then insert the two attachments together into the mouth, holding the head of the instrument beneath between her thighs; then work your hand along the entire instrument as you did with the pincers equally, according to how wide you wish to open the mouth of the patient, until she gives a sign that it is enough.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all equipped with attachments, and their forms are varied; and when the physicians have them prepared, they perform their work more quickly, and are more effective for people according to their needs.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despise the instrument because you have not prepared it, for their needs are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold her breath, and then make her sneeze by using something appropriate, and hold your hands over her mouth and nose; if she jumps because of this, it is well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take a pipette and make holes in its cover, then place herbs that can open the mouth of the mare inside it, such as camomile, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia lignea, and centaury; all these herbs or some of them should be boiled or infused in water over fire; then put one end of a tube into the opening of the pot, and the other end into the mare's mouth, and hold it so that the vapor enters inside the mare; then make her sneeze as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	The second bone jumps quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment and does not yield, as the nurse should moisten her left hand in linseed oil or mastic of hellebore, and then put it into place naturally, and seek the second bone; and when she has found it, she should take it and extend it little by little straight, so that the mass does not fall during extraction; but it must be moved gently to right and left, and then drawn out; thus it will come and release itself.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the mass is tight and closed, we have described the cure to sneeze and fumigation with herbs; and if it does not yield from all that we have said, be careful not to forcibly pull it; but instead tie what is at the mouth of the mass to the woman's thigh, then administer an ointment enema as a tetrafarmakon; this will purge and reset it, and it will come out; however, if foul odor comes from the stomach and head when it purges, it may harm the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, suitable fumigations are necessary for these cases: some of the ancients have tested fumigation with fresh herb and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument used to fumigate women for the retention of their flow and menstruation is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is made of glass resembling a tube, with the narrow end placed in the body and the wider ends over the fire; and place the fumigation over the coals, and let the smoke be inhaled until it is exhausted, then start another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born without a pierced anus, instead having a small membrane: therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to pierce that membrane properly, and not too sharply with an instrument, being careful not to injure them; then apply wool moistened in wine and oil, followed by ointment until they are healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you fear that it will not stay in place, put a chain of lead through the hole, and leave his hands free, and remove it when the child wants to go to bed.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this obstruction comes from a sudden closure of a wound or an abscess; it is necessary to cut that closure: it should be treated as we have said about the lead chain.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the anus
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from inside the anus are nodations, and those that come near or between the two parts often have one fistula or more; when this nodation is old, it works, and even now retains moisture, white pus or fine blood, and sometimes these fistulas are persistent; they are known by what comes out during defecation or flatulence when the patient has a bowel movement, and occasionally a worm may come out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that penetrate to the bladder, and up to half of the shaft; and they reach to the joint of the thigh, and to the root of the belly.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows whether the fistula penetrates to the anus or not: and it is that you insert your index finger into the anus, and insert a fine needle of silk or iron into the fistula when there is no curvature.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is curvature, insert a thread of fine linen or horsehair until you feel the thread or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and no discharge, wind, or ver comes out as we have said: you know that it does not penetrate; then hurry to treat it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula reaches to the bladder or to the conduit of urine, then it leaks urine, and cannot be healed with medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it reaches to the joint of the thigh, then the swelling comes up to that place; if there is no tortuosity and the pain remains around it, then it will become a boil immediately, and medicine or ointment does no good; and in these perforated fistulas there is no cure except labor, and vanity of foolish physicians who interfere with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the case that is not perforated and is not old, there is hope for healing by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies on their back; lift their legs up to their thighs, and incline their thighs toward their belly; then insert a probe of lead or silver if there is tortuosity, until you know where the probe stops.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the fundament, then you should place your index finger there; if you sense that the skin has been pierced; and where you feel between your finger the surface or flesh, then you know it is perforated; do not tamper with it as it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One often says that some can be well healed, but this happens rarely; and the aid given is to heat the cautery subtly according to the width of the fistula, as was mentioned before; and insert it very hot into the fistula until it reaches near the fundament; and do this two or three times until you know that the unhealthy tissues are burned, which appear like a feather; and then cure with wet dressings in butter until the flesh grows back, and afterwards use an ointment to heal and mend.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus sound, it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If that cannot be otherwise for him to be sound; and if the fistula enters, but does not penetrate all the way to the bottom which is at the foundation, and there is a thick covering of flesh or fatty tissue between your thumb and the fistula, and you see the fistula under this covering of the heart; then cut from the beginning of the fistula, and push it forward until you reach the top of the fistula, and apply the cautery afterward until it reaches the head of the fistula; and the fistula will be freed and fall out; then clean the damaged flesh that looks like a bird's feather, and leave none behind.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the flesh fails you, and there is an opening between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or with a sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cauteries assemble two good things: namely, the burning of these tissues attached, and the stopping of blood and drying of moisture; then treat with moistened bandages in butter or crushed substances until the wound weeps, and heal the tissue burned in the wound; then treat the wound with hardening ointments made from solid ingredients.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes up from deep within the anus and is distant from the body, make a poultice of it and treat it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent and it is between two layers of tissue or flesh, and it is close to piercing through, there must be no hesitation in proceeding with one of the three methods: either cauterize as we have said, cut it down to the base, or if you can place a bandage and treat it as initially instructed; do not go too deep that you might cut into the tissue holding the anus, and let evacuations occur naturally; then treat it as we have described; perhaps it will heal, or remove the covering once it has been cut near the anus, whether by dressing or another appropriate instrument; then clean the affected tissue in the wound as much as possible; then work to restore the wound and keep the fistula outside of the anus: this is a lighter task for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes there are fistulas in this manner: and it is when you insert the probe into the fistula, and it reaches the bottom of the foundation near the skin above, then take a probe perforated at the tip according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And you wind the thread in a twist from I to II, and insert the probe along the entire length of the thread into the fistula until it reaches the tip.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is passing through the margin of the foundation inside, then draw out the thread from that passage, such that you press your finger into the foundation; and pull the tip of the thread, and bring the two ends together, and hold them tightly to each other, and leave it for one or two days; and tighten it at times until the thread cuts through the flesh between them and they heal; then treat the wound until it is sealed and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not open, pierce it in all ways that you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not appropriate to cut too deeply for the treatment and then care for it as we have said until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spatumile spine from which one makes the fistula is very sharp on one side and cutting; and not so on the other side, for that which should not be cut must not be cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	for hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: those that are inside the anus, like grains of resin, and they can be small or large, and have blood in them, and there may be one or several; some are near the anus and at the head of the anus; but those farther away contain less moisture, and often a little yellow liquid or a little blood, and their color is that of the skin. The treatment for these inside the anus is to instruct the patient to sit in baths until the hemorrhoids swell out, so they can be seen clearly; then quickly grasp them with your fingernail, and cut them at their roots; if hooks cannot hold them due to moisture, use a cloth or cotton or a piece of camel wool; then pull them out with your fingers, and cut them, and sprinkle warm powders used for cautery on top; cauterize as described in the chapter on cautery, then treat further until healed; if the anus cannot be opened, administer a harsh enema to cleanse what is inside the anus so it can come out freely; when the patient feels better, and if the threads have come out of the anus, treatment is easier; grasp them with your fingernail or with forceps, cut them, then treat as we said until healed, and fear incision with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	So you should treat the suture in this manner: take twisted thread and put it on a needle, then pull the thread above and have the needle pierce from another side, and twist both ends of the thread under the needle, and let it be loose; and tightly draw the thread, then tie the thread, remove the needle, and do so for all others, leaving one to drain excess blood; then place a moist cloth dipped in rose oil or cerate on the foundation, and put it on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest; and then leave them until they defecate, and when they have done so, cure them with ointment and other treatments until they are healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	from the dryness of the feces or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often there is dryness of feces in the intestine, and by the constraint of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	You should cut with the point of a scalpel or your nail on the surface above it, without letting it moisten; then treat it until it is dry as needed; and if it cannot become dry, you should shave more forcefully than before, until it bleeds much and becomes inflamed; then treat it until it heals.
dou fremit	with trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formice is a small itchy rash on the body, and spreads very quickly; and sometimes the cold causes it, and one feels it like death from trembling, and it comes over the whole body, and more in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the treatment is that you take a thread from a goose feather or a strong vulture feather, and place the thread around the boil so that it encircles the boil completely; then turn your hand along the entire length of the thread until you cut around the boil entirely, and remove the boil by its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, do this with a thread of linen or iron according to this form, and let it be fine underneath and drawn over:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, to hold the hairs in place and press them, And if you wish, cauterize the boil as mentioned earlier in the chapter on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes a douche of silver or buckthorn is made, or of melted brass or oatmeal; and sometimes these instruments are made small and large, according to those to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those who are treated in the care of children and those who are weak and painful are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the douche, small and large, is as follows, wide, where the belly is bound in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there should be a space where the belly is bound as you see, and the tip should be pierced inside; and on one side it has two holes, and on the other side one hole; and let the belly, in which the medicine is placed from an animal bladder or parchment, be pierced all around with small holes, and there should be one digit of space between each hole, then insert a strong thread through these holes twisted ten times or so, and tie up the belly like a goat; and when the medicine is inside, attach it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then administer the douche; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head with a poultice of oil or oak leaves, or something similar, then cover it gently; then lift up the patient's head with both hands as much as possible, then remove the poultice, and raise the patient’s legs against the wall, and if the medicine needs to come out, hold it in for as long as he can; and if he sleeps a full night, it is greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you give him an enema in a case of diarrhea, and the medicine hastens to come out, then repeat it until he is well.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are at the fundament or abscessed, then let the enema be as fine as for a child; and this is the form of the fine enema in which the skin is stretched:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already discussed in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatments of hands and medicines, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are from falling on stones, and cutting with a sword or knife, or lance or staff or arrow, or similar things; they are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or foot, or belly, or liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and begin with simple wounds of the head, because the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, take care if it is from falling of stones or similar things, and the skin is entirely torn and the wound large, and you suspect the formation of a hot abscess: then I treat it immediately with the cephalic method if there is little blood coming from the wound, and let the dressing be contrary to the injured part; and prevent the patient from overindulgence in wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not wish to be bled, then reduce his meat intake, and let him drink no wine or eat flesh; and place on the wound, if hot abscesses come, cotton soaked in rose oil only, or in styptic wine; and if there is no hot abscess, then apply to the fresh wound, if it has not been exposed to air, powder, which I will mention a little later; and if inflammation has affected it, then apply some ointments until he is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar ones, and the edges cannot be brought together by stitching, then sew them together, as I will explain for belly wounds and suturing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed bone and can only be held together at one point, cut it away; then treat the wound with medicine, and replace hard flesh where leather was, and instruct the patient to eat hearty foods, such as brains and boiled wheat, like porridge, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find putrid flesh on the skin that adheres not to the bone, cut it away entirely, then apply a poultice and treat it; and if there is an artery or vein in the wound that cannot be stopped by medicines, tie off the vessel, and if you find it dislocated, mend it with thread; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is easy: it is that you put in this powder which seals as soon as the heat has drawn it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.
