And the method of the powder is as follows: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; quicksilver three parts, and mix the powder finely, and apply it to the wound, and press it firmly until it adheres well and joins with all its blood; and then tie it tightly, and do not loosen it unless it swells; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one does this with quicksilver alone, when one does not have the incense or the dragon's blood, but that the heat has drawn the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound has moved or changed, especially in summer, do not apply this powder; but put on some prepared ointments, or poultices made of barley flour mixed with water and honey, until it discharges pus; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine forceps; and I will tell you about head fractures hereafter.
de la plaie dou col	of the neck wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is on the neck and it is simple, there is no difference compared to a head wound, but if the neck nerve or artery is severed.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerve, then there should be no treatment other than leaving it alone and not applying anything constricting, for this harms the nerves and causes them to retreat; and do not apply anything cold to the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest part of the body; but let the medicine be warm, such as hot water mixed with sweet water, and rose oil, and boiled wool also in sweet water, and other minerals according to this method, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then stitch and bandage it, then treat it until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and filled with pus, then open them at the lowest point; and if an artery is cut, causing blood to flow out, then open it, ligate it, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the spine in the throat is cut, or the windpipe, and the path for air is blocked, then stitch the wound above the windpipe, but do not touch the throat, only reset it according to its natural shape; and then compress it gradually, and leave it for some days, then treat it with drying ointments until it heals; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then reduce it; and if there are pieces of bone, remove them forcefully as much as you can, and those that you cannot remove, leave them until the wound becomes pus-filled, then separate and align the exit points; and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle on the powder I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is an abscess, treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a spear or knife, and the wound is deep, then look to see if windiness comes out of the wound along with the blood: you will know that the wound is fatal; but if it is not deep, and the blood flows fresh throughout, do not put powder on it at first, nor bind it for the blood that does not come from a great depth, as it could return to the heart and kill the patient; instead, apply an adhesive ointment, and change the bandage twice a day. And if you have no ointment, place old cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture, and allow the patient to rest on the wound for three days, or four, or more; this way, there will be no spasm, nor trembling, nor strangeness of breath; and when you see good signs, you will know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat it then with tents and other treatments until he is healed; and if it cannot be healed, operate, and you will know that there is an abscess; treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple, whether on the front or back, treat it like any other; if it is large, stitch it up; and if it is small, apply powder, and if it is pressed against the bone, and has severed pieces, then cleanse the wound, and repair torn tendons; and if they are not torn, let the wound heal on its own, which will ease the extraction of foreign bodies; and for other wounds on other limbs, judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the abdomen is great and medium and small; from the large wound sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines protrude, leading to intestinal perforation; and the suturing is more difficult. Sometimes a smaller wound is worse than a larger one because if the intestines are not returned frequently, they are pushed back in too much at once; for when they feel cold, they swell immediately and are pushed back in harder, so a smaller wound can be better, as it allows the intestine to return gently to its place more often. And you should know that there are four types of rupture: two common sutures happen with abdominal suturing, and the other two specific to other wounds; yet all are particularly suited for abdominal sutures, and I will describe each one and explain them.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and some part of the intestine protrudes, and it is a difficult thing to replace, this can be done in one of two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or some thin cloth with hot water only, which you cook with hot vinegar and cypress and spikenard, and rinse the intestine until the swelling subsides; and sometimes use wine that constricts to make it less swollen.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with water in which hellebore and mallows have been cooked, for this gradually opens the entrance; and if it cannot enter, make a small incision in the wound with the instrument used to cut hemorrhoids; and the first treatment should be such that one does not cut unless there is great necessity; and here is the tool for making the incision: cut inward along the curvature without going out, and see here the form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines jump out, place them back according to their natural form in their proper place if you have the power, for that is better.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the back part of the abdomen, you should have the patient lie on their back with their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the front part of the abdomen, raise the head and feet higher than the affected area; and also if there is a rupture of the abdomen in one of the two parts, arrange so that the injured part is higher than the other; and thus should be treated what I say about large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	In small wounds, apply what is appropriate to you, then hold a minister who holds the entire wound with their hand and brings together the edges; this is the common method of suturing. Take one or more needles according to the width of the wound, leaving an inch at the beginning of the wound before inserting the needle with strong thread; pierce both sides of the skin with the two inner layers of tissue beneath it until you have pierced through the entire section, and bring together the four corners; then twist a double thread around the needle on both sides, and then join the two edges of the wound, leaving an inch of space before inserting another needle. Tie the knot of the thread as you did with the first needle, and continue this process until the entire wound is sutured; the needles should be medium-sized, between fine and thick, because too thin needles cut through all flesh, and overly thick ones cannot enter properly: thus they should be medium-sized; do not insert the needles too far from the skin and tissue so as to damage the wound before it heals; then cut the ends of the needles short so that they do not hurt the patient when sleeping, and place cloth or fabric over them for protection until the wound is healed. This method of needle suturing is more suitable for small wounds, but a second common technique involves bringing together both sides of the skin and tissue on one needle with strong thread; once you have pierced all four corners, tie off the needle as you would sew fabric; leave an inch between each stitch. A person can do this suture method, and I myself stitched up a wound that someone had in their abdomen which was cut by a knife, larger than a palm's width, with intestines protruding two palms' length from inside the belly, located right at the center of the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned the intestine to its place after it had been outside for twenty-four hours, and the wound was sealed up until fifteen days, and I treated it, and he was well.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the doctors had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicines; and I placed old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he was well.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper methods of suturing: take the needle, and pierce from the outer part to the inner; when it has pierced straight through the skin, place the head of the suture where you have inserted the needle, and make it pierce again from the inner part to the outer; and the understanding of this suture is that you sew as the tailor does with furs, and leave once the side on one side, and return to it from the other, until the entire suture is completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of suturing, which Galen describes properly, is as follows: one joins the two parts naturally together, and applies one end to the other in such a way: insert a needle at the nearest chief part of the muscle, piercing only that spot while leaving the two ends of the suture; then turn the needle and pierce from the outer part inward through both ends of the suture; then pierce each side from the outer part inward through two more parts of the muscle on the opposite side; and this is the safest method of suturing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen says this and some attest that one should sew the abdomen with two needles, each having thread; and one must insert one needle from one side and the other from the opposite side, in the manner of those who sew belts; and note that when the rupture is inside the abdomen, the suture is more difficult than in other parts of the abdomen.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is like the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, as if the flesh has not been moved, then reset the intestines, and sew; then put on healing powder, and if the flesh has been moved, then apply any ointment that is present until the wound heals; and stitch the wound, and let the sifac and the muscle heal together; then treat the wound like others, until it is healthy; and if you do not have medicines, then place old cotton as soon as it begins to discharge pus, and change it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need other medicines in many cases where the wounds are simple; and if you fear that the wound may affect the principal members, it is necessary to moisten light wool in heated rose oil or olive oil, and place it around the angles and under the armpits; and if there is pain or putrefaction in the bowels, which often happens, then administer a black tea enema of wine, especially if the putrefaction reaches the intestines; and pierce inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it heals more easily than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine called "jejunum" cannot heal when it is pierced, and this is because of the smallness of the veins that are there, and because of the subtlety of the entire body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the spleen jumps out of the wound, put it back as you would with the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has turned green or black, then tie off the black area so that no blood seeps through, because there are veins and arteries; then cut around the ligature and hang both ends from below the wound to facilitate extraction when the spleen falls out, and the wound will heal.
de la routure dou boueil	of the fracture of the eye socket
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is cut and the wound is small, it can sometimes be restored in some people, for I saw a man pierced in the belly with a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, from which excretions and gases issued; I treated it according to what I could, and did not stop suturing until he was healed, and the flesh grew together.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it heal, I feared the patient would have pain in his belly; but he felt no discomfort and improved in health, eating and drinking normally. And some experienced practitioners say that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be treated as follows: take large-headed clamps, then bring together the edges of the wound, and when the clamp opens its jaws, place them over the two edges so they press tightly; then cut off the head, and this holds fast so it cannot come undone. Do this successively in the same manner until the entire wound is closed, and sew the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the head of the intestine is inflamed and causes no harm to the patient, it can be tied with a fine thread that matches the intestine of an animal in this way: take the tip of this intestinal thread which is very clean, then wrap around it a thin linen thread tightly, then put the thread on the needle, and sew the intestine, and pull it together at the wound; and this method of stitching does no harm except according to the path of trust and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the main intestines, there is no remedy or cure unless with subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it matures, is generally called a "fistula," especially when it has become hollow and sinks inward.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to the truth an improper knot hard and white, where one does not feel pain, and it is also feathered like the quill of a bird; and sometimes it swells clear, and other times thick; sometimes pus is little, and other times enough; and I have already spoken in the division of wounds that every wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, except for one of the IX causes: namely, because of the smallness of the blood or body; or because of its malice; or because there is hard flesh within, and on the lips, which does not allow new flesh to grow; or there is too much pus; or the place is rotten, and the matter has poor quality; or the medicine used for treatment is not good; or because corruption resembles a pestilence; or because the property in the region is slow digestion, and late healing, and swollen by nature; or there are veins in the bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and signs, and treatments of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary for me to tell you about the treatment of a fistula which is done by hand work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	You should know that fistulas can occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or on the surface, or in the intestine, or bladder, or some ribs, or spine, or joints of the hands or feet; and some affect the principal part of a limb, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are of this kind are difficult to heal, except through labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not reach the places I have mentioned, and you trust in its treatment, and you wish to know it, take a probe of brass or iron, if the fistula is straight, and insert it; and if the fistula is curved, use a delicate probe made of lead, because lead can be bent around the curvature; and if the fistula has multiple openings and you cannot properly explore it with probes, inject through one of the openings, for moisture passes from one opening to another, and cleanse it; then gently press it within your power to know if there is bone or nerve inside, and feel thoroughly, and ask the patient carefully about the pain they feel when pressed by your hand, and where they feel it; and when you truly know the location of it, and whether it is far from a joint, nerve, artery, vein, or any of the places I have mentioned, cut it out according to what I have said, and remove the unhealthy flesh that is inside; then treat it until it heals, and if the fistula is deeply straight, you must cut it thoroughly as much as possible, then insert moistened probes in a medicinal acid to corrode the excess left at the bottom; and then apply healing ointments for healthy tissue until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this means, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, cut it out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not trouble the principal limbs as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackening, then cut away until all corruption is removed, then cure it with applications of flesh-restoring substances until it is healthy; and if it is not healthy, and returns to its original state as before, know that you have not reached the depth: uncover and search until you reach the bottom, remove all corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healthy, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach; there is no other remedy but to leave it to nature; and if there is a small corrupt bone that you can pull with forceps, extract it with suitable instruments, and if there are many bones, remove them all without leaving any; and if the moisture opposes you, and there is no error or fear, cut away both corruption and flesh, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them at once, place on the wound something that promotes putrefaction, and leave it until the flesh is rotten around the bones, and then the bones will be more easily removed; and if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh, cut away only the corruption until all black matter is removed, then restore the wound; and if there is much corrupted part remaining, reaching to the bone marrow; you must scrape and cut away all the corruption, and then cure it until it is healed; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened in a man's leg, so take this as an example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg due to something that came inside the body, so that the substances reached the leg and it swelled with a large abscess, and there was no reason for it to burst on its own; but the physicians, out of their foolishness, operated excessively until they opened the abscesses and removed much matter from them, and it became a fistula, and many holes appeared through which all humors and moisture of the body flowed; and several doctors treated him for two years, and no one had any skill in the art of hands, until I was called to see him, and saw his leg and the medicines used to treat him, as well as what came out through the openings in large quantities; and the young man's skin turned red, and he had a yellowish complexion.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these holes, and then searched all the holes, and found that they came against each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then hurried and cut into one of the holes until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and perforated, with the corruption reaching inside the bone; I cleansed what appeared to be the corrupted bone, thinking there was no further corruption besides that which I removed; and began to treat the wound with astringent medicines over a long period, but it could not heal; then I started again, cut into the bone as before, found the corruption continuing in the bone, cleaned it out, removed it, and tried to close the place; but I was only able to do so around one palm's width of the bone, treated it until it was completely healed, and then applied medicines to close it; and it quickly became healthy and closed, and there was no need to start over except for the patient's weakness, which could not bear it, and out of fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For although the evacuation of blood was often done, he remained entirely healthy, and in place of the bone grew hard flesh, and he had good constitution and suffered no harm or contraindication at all, neither going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated as follows: take some linen, and pull it at the end of the visible bone, and have someone stretch it upwards; and place another piece of coarser flax over the skin covering the bone, and extend the top so that you draw the corrupted flesh inward, and expose the flesh where you wish to treat, so that the poultice does not damage the flesh; and put a cautery or a table beneath the bone to remove the corrupted flesh; and continue to treat until one can see and feel no more corruption, and treat again if necessary.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and it appears so, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part of it, then uncover all the flesh; then place a firebrand underneath, and then use silk from one side to the other for the corruption, and let the length of the silk be as we have said; and if the corruption is at the joint, then cut off the corrupted joint, and suture the bone on the other part; and if the corruption is between two joints, there is no remedy but cutting; and if the corruption is in the finger or toe, it is very severe, yet you must inquire into that corrosion as it appears to you; and clean it by all means possible, but do not let the vein or nerve oppose you; and know that the instruments for cutting these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and their appearance, and their size and fineness, and their length and shortness, and hardness; therefore you must prepare an instrument suitable for each kind of work; and know that your work will show you which tool you need, according to your knowledge of this art and the evidence of the manner of diseases; so consider the instrument you need according to what is necessary.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The head may rot from within or from without; and when you have treated that corruption with medicine but it does not help, then you must amputate the limb at the place where the corruption begins, so that the patient escapes either death or the greater evil of losing the limb; and the sign is that the limb turns black as if burned by fire, and rots after turning black, for this corruption spreads from limb to limb and takes over the whole body; therefore hasten to amputate it, and if this is due to a venomous creature's bite, such as a sea scorpion or a viper and similar, and the corruption reaches the head of the arm, then cut it off and do not give it time to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes to the hand, cover at the joint, so that the corrosion does not reach the arm; and if it comes to the arm, cut with a knife; and if it passes the knife, it is death, and there is no remedy except for the quantity of its power; and do all this as well when corruption comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, cover after the second joint; and if it comes to the foot, cover the whole foot; and if it climbs up the leg, cover at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy but to let the patient die; and the way of cutting or covering the limb is that you tie above and below, and extend one minister with a ligature downwards, and another minister upwards, and cut the flesh between the two ligatures at one span wide, until the bone is uncovered; then cut or cauterize it, and place a strip of linen on each side so that the cauterization does not touch healthy skin and cause another injury or abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs while you are working, cauterize the area quickly or apply some powders that constrict; then return to your medicine until it is completed, and bind the injured limb with an appropriate bandage, and treat it until it heals; and I will tell you what happened to a man in such cases: he suffered from a blackness which seemed like a burn by fire, and this corrosion started on his big toe first, spreading to cover his entire foot; when the man saw the corrosion, he hastened to amputate his foot, and was healed; and after some time, the corrosion returned at the thumb of his hand, and he came to me, and I applied repelling substances after cleansing his body, but could not stop the corruption; and he decided that I should cut off his hand, and I refused because I hoped to repel the matter; also feared that if I cut his hand, he would die, since his strength was weak; and in despair, he returned home and amputated his hand himself, and healed; and I have not been satisfied with anything except for those who act differently when there is a need.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess appears in the flesh and remains so long that it forms a large collection of pus; then it ruptures and drains, leaving behind a cavity like a vessel; and the skin above is as thin as fine cloth, not extending to the bone or nerve; such a disease is called "sain" and is not called "fistula"; but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone completely, then it is called "fistula"; and the skin can be cut around entirely, even when it is thin like cloth; and it does not adhere due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you trust that the skin adheres and the corruption is not complete, and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it with a clister as follows: check if the breast is large and the pus coming from it has a foul odor; then administer an Egyptian medicine clister in this manner: take equal parts of myrrh, oil, and litharge, put them to heat in a container over fire until they turn red and become as thick as honey; then use this according to your need, mix it with water and honey or wine, and administer the clister while holding back the anus; let the medicine remain inside for two hours, then expel it gently; do this repeatedly until the breast is cleansed of its foulness; if the patient cannot tolerate this, or Egyptian medicine is unavailable, use a mixture of water and honey with a little ground litharge; or you can administer a clister made from honey and mixed wine where honey has cleansing properties and wine aids in adhering the skin; once this is done and you trust that the breast is thoroughly cleansed, then administer something that promotes flesh growth such as an emollient plaster made of rose oil and vinegar, or other medicines and ointments whose properties I have discussed when treating ointments; if the opening for the clister is too small, enlarge it slightly with a probe and place a dressing of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it fits; and if the wound is too wide, suture it leaving only an area where the clister can enter; if the pus discharging passage is above, cut lower down where there isn't such discharge.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bowe is deep, it does not allow flesh to regenerate; and if you cannot cut the breast as desired, prepare in such a way that the bowe flows downward to the lowest place where it is. For when the bowe is deep, it does not allow flesh to regenerate and if you cannot cut the breast as desired, prepare in this manner: so that the bowe flows slightly downwards, leaving nothing of the bowe; then take consolidating medicines to put on the healthy part, and stretch a piece of linen cloth covering all the healthy area; then cut at the forceful place the aperture of the breast one bit wider than the first, and spread an ointment according to the size of the aperture over the aperture of the wound to alleviate the bowe, and do not remove the large cloth outside until after several days once; and that which is on the aperture of the breast, take often to remove the bowe, and know what flows from the bowe, whether it is venom or little or enough, or digestible, or indigestible; and be wary if the patient feels pain or not, and whether there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been extended in this manner and you see the nature that jumps over the aperture of the wound, know that the healing is now beginning, and approach health; and then loosen it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you loosen the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the stomach throws up undigested food after many days, know that the stomach does not settle.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle venom is cut after a long time, do not despair of the health, for health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are people for whom food heals their wounds slowly, and others who do the opposite; and if undigested food comes up from the stomach after many days, know that the stomach does not settle; and if digestion is delayed and prolonged, add medicines that are dry in substance but moist in virtue, such as a diaphoretic ointment, for it contains a large part of vitriol, and this is the last medicine to use; take a diaphoretic ointment made with rose oil, and dilute it equally with old wine; then boil it and use it; and the same thing works better when thickened if no diaphoretic ointment is present: take murre, aloes, and incense, grind them together, and mix them with honey over a fire; then glue a cloth on it and apply it to the stomach; sometimes administer a long strip of aristology and celestial lily roots, which are like fine wheat and centaury flour; use either simple or compound preparations: grind them into powder and mix with the honey I mentioned and use it; if treatment is prolonged and ineffective, then know that corruption has reached perfection and imprinted on the bone, or in hard members or tendons; then treat according to the method for fistula as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panaritis is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the finger or toe, or sometimes in other toes; and when it ages and is not attended to, a foul abscess comes, running and discharging pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and perhaps running through entirely; and the corruption reaches the bone, causing putrid pain, and the head of the toe becomes swollen, and its color turns black.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment is of no use, then you must cut away all the excess that remains around the nail, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a great aid if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy; and if the nail presses on the flesh, causing it to become inflamed and ulcerated, then you must place the blade under the nail that pierces the flesh, raise it up, and cut away the affected flesh carefully and lightly, then apply the remaining flesh with burning and corrosive medicines to remove everything; finally cure it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut it out and pull out the pus, for as long as the corroded part of the bone remains, it cannot heal; and if you see that the bone is corrupted, cut it off from one side as was previously mentioned, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is pierced and the patient feels great pain, you must first treat it; then carefully trim the nail diagonally with a sharp instrument, being careful not to cut into the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if this happens, apply something that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the swelling of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The second joints that are born in some people's hands by chance are all flesh, and sometimes there are bones in them, and at times a nail is present, and some of them are born at the root of the joint, where the origin is in some places in the flesh.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those who are born with any nodule on the finger do not move, and those who are born at the joint of the finger may sometimes move; the size of the one that is fleshy is so slight, in this manner: measure it from its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those who are born at the root of the joint are difficult to treat: be careful when cutting them.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who is born or should be at the back part, you must first cut away the flesh roundly until reaching the bone, then cut the bone in a single stroke suitable for that person, then treat it until it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The union that comes to the two bones together comes by birth, or by healing of a wound, or by burning with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	You must cut away that union so that the bones can heal according to their natural forms; then place between them two cloths or towels moistened in rose oil so they do not unite again; or put between two pieces of fine lead until the wound is healed as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If the union comes to either of them with the palm, you must cut that union as it should be done.
des vils	of worms
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are thick, enveloped, full of melancholic excesses that occur in many parts of the body; and they happen more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry loads than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer enemas to them at times, and then treat them with basilicon ointment.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment with iron is according to two methods: one is that you cut it and draw out the black blood; and the other method is that you open the vein and draw all the blood out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The treatment with the lancet is according to this method: first apply a hot water bath very strongly to the leg until the thick blood becomes thin, then strain the patient's leg from above the thigh down to the area below the knee; then cut the vein in one place or two or three, making a broad incision, and then draw out the black blood with your hand from one side to the other, as much blood as the strength of the patient can endure; then dress it, and instruct him to eat food that induces purging; and repeat the evacuation and treatment when the veins are full, but do not harm the patient at night.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The lifting of the vein is done in this manner: raise the patient's leg if it has much hair, then place it in a bath, and bathe the leg with hot water until it becomes red and the veins swell; and if you do not have a bath, heat it by fire, and then cut directly along the long vein from the top of the knee to below the ankle or at the part above the instep; then work the skin with a scalpel, and strip off the vein on each side until it feels firm when touched; and one can see it as red and black, and when it enters the skin it appears like a white cord; then lift the vein underneath, and comb it gently with an uncine, as you did before, and cut another length or more if necessary, then raise it again and cut at the toe joint, pull and lift up to the second length; then strip it from one length to the next until it comes out entirely, and then cut it; and if you cannot pull and lift it, pierce the thread along its entire length with a needle, tie and pull it, place another stitch underneath, and move your hand back and forth until it is done; take care that it does not break because if it breaks, it cannot be pulled or lifted, which would harm the patient; when you have finished pulling it entirely, put on the wound site wool soaked in wine and rose oil; dress the wound until it heals.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it sharply, but do not sever it; and draw it out as we have previously stated.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the knife used to cut the vein is curved, and it does not cut through, so as not to sever the vein; and it is thickly curved, because if it were fine, it would cut the vein, but it should be thick as we have said, and this is its form:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in the legs, in warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in dry ground that lacks moisture; and by chance it may appear elsewhere than in the legs, and this occurs due to putrefaction beneath the skin, as it spreads within the body like serpents and worms, growing between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that there comes a very great inflammation in the leg, then it changes its place, and the vein begins to come out as if from a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein is open, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of cloth from one and a half to two fingers wide, tie it, and leave the cloth hanging down the leg, and every time there is an excess point coming out, then wrap it around the cloth and tie it; if it is too long, cut off part of it, and wrap the remainder, but do not cut it at its root until it comes out completely; for if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh and cause abscesses and corruption in that place, and a bad disease; because such things must be treated little by little until there is nothing left on the body; sometimes this vein when treated is five palms long or ten, and once it happened to me with one who had it issuing out ten palms long, and when you cut it, let one row or hole come out so that everything comes out; and empty the matter inside, then administer medicine there for corruption for some days, then treat it as abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes this vein branches off, especially when it appears at the ankle joint or near the foot, where there is much perforation and from which it branches again; treat it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that are born between the skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "buffalo disease," because it often affects buffaloes, and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, and travels throughout the body moving up and down, and people feel it well as it moves from limb to limb, until it breaks the skin where it goes, causing pain; and it arises from putrid humors, such as worms, serpents, lice, and ascarids in the belly; and one fears its malice, because when it travels through the body, if it ascends to the head, and comes to the eye, by chance it enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it necessary to cure and drain it, one cannot do so forcefully: therefore, tie the area above and below with a strong tight bandage, then cut over it and draw out the pus; if the vein is deep in the flesh and you cannot find it, cauterize it with fire until it closes; and the greatest harm it can cause is that it may affect the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming near the eye at the head, hold firmly below it the eyebrow, then cut over it, and draw out the pus; and the patient should use cleansing of body with dissolving medicines for purging bad humors, and avoid eating inflammatory foods.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from gas or windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to certain limbs, and can move from one limb to another; and I have seen what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, where I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and shortly after, I saw it rise as quickly as a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything, like quicksilver when it flows from one place to another; the pain departed from that spot and settled in the shoulder, and then a short while later spread throughout her body until it reached the other arm; she told me that it kept circling around her body quickly, as I had seen.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly at how it moved from limb to limb, for I had never seen this disease in such a manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I have seen many who wished to move pain from one place to another, but I did not want it, as I saw in the woman; and I thought that was because she had dry flesh, and veins uncovered, and therefore this windiness appears constrained; and they do not appear according to this reason in those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and veins covered.
