And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the affected leg quickly, as I have said; and place the physician's hand on the affected side, then press with the other hand, and stretch towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is to the side, one should not extend the affected leg downward or lift it up off the ground, but rather place it as if the hip were dislocated to the side, as we have said about lying on both hips; and let him lie on his face, with the limb extended as we have stated previously, and press on the joint against a table; it is done properly when the patient extends their legs equally; then join the thighs together, apply a plaster, and secure them with a bandage so that the hip does not move; rest for three or four days, then remove the bandage, and reapply the plaster; if they are still equal, secure them again as before, and leave it for three days; then release the bandage and allow him to walk gently until his limb is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: namely, inward and outward, and backward; it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are such that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at his thigh, and if it does not bend at the thigh, then you know it is dislocated; and the restoration of all these cases is that you have the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back against his back, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and pull between your hands, then bend the two sides of the knee firmly; and another assistant extends his foot, so that the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that it bends well at the thigh lightly; and apply a plaster, and bind the leg to the thigh tightly for three days or four, then unbind him; and do not let the patient work on walking until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not properly aligned, apply strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the thigh, until it is healed
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes bruised, and sometimes completely dislocated, both internally and externally.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and tense in the area where it is dislocated; the reduction is light, and one should gently extend it with their hands when it is only bruised.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, you must have the patient sit upright, and hold him firmly by the thigh with your hand above the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, then twice with your left, then extend upwards, and forcefully push the foot upwards; do this twice as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, continue the work, for it will come back; and if it cannot return thus, make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and firmly place a lever between his thighs, tying ropes around him so he does not move; then hold one thigh with your hand, another assistant extends the foot with their hands or uses a strap to secure it at the ankle; both assistants extend equally, and the lever remains steady between the patient's thighs to restrain the patient when extending; then place the dislocation in your hands equally, and have another assistant hold the healthy leg behind, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is ready, place the poultice and plugs on it, bind it firmly, tie the foot to the leg, and watch the nerves above the heel so that the bandage is not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the binding loosens, tighten it; then untie it on the third day or fourth, and forbid the patient from walking for four days; and if he walks before this term, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if foot abscesses come, you must treat them as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	of the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When both are dislocated, they must be gently extended without strain, and this is an easy task.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is at any joint of the foot's back, it is necessary that you make the patient sit on a level spot or on a .ie. table straight, and place your foot under what appears of these joints, then press with your foot firmly, until it returns; and when they are equal, and there does not appear anything, put under the sole of the foot a board of II fingers, then strain firmly, and leave for III days, then release; and make them rest, until they are healthy.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation and one wishes to restore it, many times the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in treatment if you are not wise in the art and have not used it for long, and if you are not pitiful and merciful and cautious, not bold; and use at the beginning soothing things for hot abscesses, and leave the patient in God's hands if there is no hope of health; and when you see hope, now set the limb in place as though hot abscesses would come; and when the limb is in place, administer soothing things for hot abscesses, and treat the wound with ointments as is appropriate; and if along with dislocation there is a fracture and small bones displaced, remove them and do what we have said about simple diseases; and guard against entering the path of fear according to what I have said, because it befits you more according to your Creator, and for the knowledge of your art and your body.
Amen	So be it
